class="vocs:text-sm vocs:text-secondary">January 22, 2026</time></div></div><div class="vocs:hidden vocs:md:block vocs:absolute vocs:left-36 vocs:top-8 vocs:bottom-0 vocs:ml-4 vocs:w-px vocs:border-l vocs:mb-4"><a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/releases/tag/v1.6.0-rc1" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="vocs:inline-flex vocs:items-center vocs:gap-1.5 vocs:text-sm class="vocs:text-sm vocs:text-secondary">January 22, 2026</time></div><div class="vocs:relative"><div class="vocs:prose vocs:prose-sm vocs:max-w-none vocs:overflow-hidden vocs:transition-[max-height] vocs:duration-300"><div class="vocs:space-y-6 vocs:[&amp;&gt;*:first-child]:mt-0 vocs:[&amp;&gt;*:last-child]:mb-0" data-v-content="true"><h1 data-v>Foundry v1.6.0</h1>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.6.0 brings <strong data-v>Osaka as the default EVM hardfork</strong>, major <strong data-v>performance improvements</strong> with parallelized stateless fuzzing and configurable invariant check intervals (up to 3.6x faster deep runs), enhanced <strong data-v>security testing</strong> with improved reentrancy detection and time-based invariant fuzzing, and additional <strong data-v>Tempo blockchain integration</strong> across forge, cast, and anvil.</p>
<p data-v>We recently crossed 10,000 GitHub ð â thank you to everyone who has contributed, reported issues, and helped improve Foundry!</p>
<hr data-v>
<h2 data-v>Performance</h2>
<h3 data-v>Parallelized Stateless Fuzzing (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12713" data-v>#12713</a>)</h3>
<p data-v>Fuzz tests now run across multiple worker threads, significantly improving execution speed on multi-core machines. Each worker maintains its own corpus and periodically syncs with a master corpus, enabling efficient parallel exploration while sharing discovered coverage. Workers automatically distribute runs evenly and aggregate results after completion.</p>
<h3 data-v>Invariant <code data-v>check_interval</code> Config (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13133" data-v>#13133</a>)</h3>
<p data-v>New <code data-v>check_interval</code> config option controls how often invariants are asserted during deep runs:</p>
<div data-v-table-wrapper><table data-v>
<thead data-v>
<tr data-v>
<th data-v>Value</th>
<th data-v>Behavior</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody data-v>
<tr data-v>
<td data-v><code data-v>0</code></td>
<td data-v>Only assert on the last call of each run (fastest)</td>
</tr>
<tr data-v>
<td data-v><code data-v>1</code> (default)</td>
<td data-v>Assert after every call (current behavior, most precise)</td>
</tr>
<tr data-v>
<td data-v><code data-v>N</code></td>
<td data-v>Assert every N calls AND always on the last call</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></div>
<p data-v><strong data-v>Benchmark</strong>: With <code data-v>check_interval = 10</code>, deep invariant runs (1Ã1000 depth) are <strong data-v>3.6x faster</strong> (15.09s â 4.17s). Invariant checks consume ~86% of execution time in high-depth runsâreducing check frequency dramatically improves performance while still catching violations.</p>
<h3 data-v>Other Performance Improvements</h3>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v>perf: add dist profile for smaller release binaries (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13097" data-v>#13097</a>) by @onbjerg</li>
<li data-v>perf: compute literals only once (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12716" data-v>#12716</a>) by @DaniPopes</li>
<li data-v>perf: remove redundant allocation in receipt bloom calculation (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13035" data-v>#13035</a>) by @marukai67</li>
</ul>
<hr data-v>
<h2 data-v>Security Testing</h2>
<h3 data-v>Improved Reentrancy Detection with <code data-v>call_override</code> (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13127" data-v>#13127</a>)</h3>
<p data-v>The <code data-v>call_override</code> invariant testing feature now correctly detects ETH transfer reentrancy vulnerabilities, including:</p>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v><strong data-v>EtherStore pattern</strong>: Classic DAO-style reentrancy where a handler sends ETH out and the attacker reenters</li>
<li data-v><strong data-v>Rari Capital pattern</strong>: Protocol-level reentrancy where external protocols send ETH to handlers</li>
</ul>
<p data-v>Key fixes include proper ETH transfer via journal before callback injection, clearing REVM's cached bytecode for EOA targets, and overriding calls when either caller OR target is a handler contract. Validated against a reproduction of the April 2022 Rari Capital hack.</p>
<h3 data-v>Time-based Invariant Fuzzing (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12616" data-v>#12616</a>)</h3>
<p data-v>New <code data-v>max_time_delay</code> and <code data-v>max_block_delay</code> invariant configs enable fuzzing of block timestamp and block number on consecutive transactions. This helps discover time-dependent vulnerabilities that only manifest under specific block timing conditions. Counterexamples now display the <code data-v>vm.warp()</code> and <code data-v>vm.roll()</code> calls needed to reproduce failures.</p>
<hr data-v>
<h2 data-v>Improved Integration</h2>
<h3 data-v>Foundry-toolchain TypeScript Rewrite</h3>
<p data-v>The <a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain" data-v><code data-v>foundry-toolchain</code></a> GitHub Action has been completely rewritten in TypeScript for improved maintainability and reliability. See <a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain/releases/tag/v1.7.0" data-v>v1.7.0 release</a>.</p>
<h3 data-v>Foundryup Rust Rewrite (Experimental)</h3>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.6.0 is accompanied by a new Rust rewrite of <a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundryup" data-v><code data-v>foundryup</code></a> for better maintainability, testing, and compatibility. At the moment the new <code data-v>foundryup</code> installer is still experimental, but in next releases we plan to sunset the old one and provide a much better experience for managing foundry installs.</p>
<p data-v>To try out the new <code data-v>foundryup</code> run:</p>
<pre data-v><code class="language-bash" data-v>curl -L https://raw.githubusercontent.com/foundry-rs/foundryup/HEAD/foundryup-init.sh | bash
foundryup
</code></pre>
<hr data-v>
<h2 data-v>Network Updates</h2>
<h3 data-v>Tempo Blockchain Integration</h3>
<p data-v>Additional Tempo network support is now available across the Foundry toolchain:</p>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v>feat(forge): add <code data-v>--network tempo</code> flag to <code data-v>forge init</code> (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12819" data-v>#12819</a>) by @onbjerg - Initialize projects pre-configured for Tempo</li>
<li data-v>feat(cast): tempo nonce keys (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12977" data-v>#12977</a>) by @onbjerg - Support for Tempo's nonce key system</li>
<li data-v>feat(cast): add tempo tx construction support (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12973" data-v>#12973</a>) by @onbjerg - Build and sign Tempo transactions</li>
<li data-v>feat(anvil): basic tempo tx signing support (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12974" data-v>#12974</a>) by @onbjerg - Local development with Tempo transactions</li>
<li data-v>feat(<code data-v>foundryup</code>): add Tempo support (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12775" data-v>#12775</a>) by @zerosnacks - Install Tempo-enabled Foundry builds</li>
</ul>

vocs:max-w-none vocs:overflow-hidden vocs:transition-[max-height] vocs:duration-300"><div class="vocs:space-y-6 vocs:[&amp;&gt;*:first-child]:mt-0 vocs:[&amp;&gt;*:last-child]:mb-0" data-v-content="true"><h1 data-v>Foundry v1.5.1</h1>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.1 is a bugfix release to support solc 0.8.31.</p>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v>fix: backport svm rs bump to 1.5.1 / stable (#12871) by @grandizzy</li>
</ul>
<h1 data-v>Foundry v1.5.0</h1>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 release comes with an improved fuzzer that use <a href="https://github.com/paradigmxyz/solar" data-v><code data-v>Solar</code></a> to analyze contracts and extract interested values from AST, and incorporate updated logic to minimize counterexamples generated by invariant tests. This version adds support for browser extension wallets, provides a simpler way to interact with ERC20 tokens using cast and publishes all foundry binaries as npm packages. It also continues the effort to improve new forge formatter rolled out in previous version and makes it more customizable.</p>
<h2 data-v>Fuzzed tests improvements</h2>
<h3 data-v>AST seeded dictionary</h3>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 leverages the Solar API to analyze contracts, collect all relevant AST literals from the sources, and use those values to generate inputs for the fuzzing campaign (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12015" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12015</a>).
For example, with this addition a counterexample for the simple test below can be generated within a couple of runs:</p>
<pre data-v><code class="language-Solidity" data-v>function testHash(bytes memory v) external {
    assert(keccak256(v) != keccak256("hello"));
}
</code></pre>
<p data-v>Early testers have reported substantially improved fuzzing results and we are running additional benchmarks to quantify the effectiveness.</p>
<h3 data-v>Improved counterexample shrinking</h3>
<p data-v>In previous versions, counterexamples generated by invariant tests were replayed and minimized only once. In Foundry v1.5.0, the call sequence is replayed multiple times until all configured shrink runs are completed (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12180" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12180</a>). Additionally, the counterexamples saved on disk and replayed on subsequent campaigns, are now also minimized (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12351" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12351</a>). This allows Foundry to produce a more thoroughly minimized call sequence that can be used to generate unit tests and reproduce smart contract invariant violations.</p>
<h2 data-v>Browser wallet integration</h2>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 introduces support for browser extension wallets in the <code data-v>cast send</code> and <code data-v>cast wallet sign</code> commands, enabling developers to sign transactions directly in the browser (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12302" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12302</a>). Future releases will expand browser wallet support to other Foundry commands. We look forward to get external contributions to improve <a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-browser-wallet" data-v>the interface</a> and feature set of the browser wallet.</p>
<p data-v>To try it out, pass the <code data-v>--browser</code> flag to <code data-v>cast send</code> to send a transaction using any of your browser wallets: <code data-v>cast send &#x3C;TO> --value &#x3C;VALUE> --rpc-url &#x3C;RPC_URL> --browser</code></p>
<p align="center">
  <img width="441" height="492" alt="Porto send" src="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/850a2108-15e1-484c-987f-208b3c2ececf" />
</p>
<p data-v>Additionally you can sign messages and typed data with <code data-v>cast wallet sign</code>: <code data-v>cast wallet sign --browser "Hello World!"</code></p>
<p align="center">
  <img width="441" height="492" alt="Porto Sign" src="https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/2ff1fbbc-b565-4182-9993-6c640783c575" />
</p>
<h2 data-v>ERC20 support in cast</h2>
<p data-v>This release introduces the <code data-v>cast erc20</code> command to facilitate interaction with ERC-20 tokens (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12258" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12258</a> <a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12381" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12381</a>). This makes it simple to query balances, perform transfers, and access other ERC-20 token details.</p>
<pre data-v><code class="language-bash" data-v>  balance       Query ERC20 token balance [aliases: b]
  transfer      Transfer ERC20 tokens [aliases: t]
  approve       Approve ERC20 token spending [aliases: a]
  allowance     Query ERC20 token allowance [aliases: al]
  name          Query ERC20 token name [aliases: n]
  symbol        Query ERC20 token symbol [aliases: s]
  decimals      Query ERC20 token decimals [aliases: d]
  total-supply  Query ERC20 token total supply [aliases: ts]
  mint          Mint ERC20 tokens (if the token supports minting) [aliases: m]
  burn          Burn ERC20 tokens [aliases: bu]
</code></pre>
<h2 data-v>New cheatcodes</h2>
<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 includes a set of new cheatcodes designed to improve the testing experience:</p>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v><code data-v>getEvmVersion/setEvmVersion</code> to retrieve and change the execution EVM version within tests and scripts (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12014" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12014</a>)</li>
<li data-v><code data-v>signWithNonce</code> to create deterministic ECDSA signatures using a specified ephemeral nonce (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11267" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11267</a>)</li>
<li data-v><code data-v>getStorageSlots</code> leverage the storage layout to accurately identify the base slot of a variable (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11537" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11537</a>)</li>
</ul>
<h2 data-v>npm packages</h2>
<p data-v>Continuing the work introduced in v1.4.0 for <code data-v>forge</code>, v1.5.0 publishes the remaining Foundry binaries as npm packages. This allows tools such as <code data-v>bun</code>, <code data-v>npx</code>, <code data-v>pnpm</code> to easily install and run any Foundry executable directly from the npm registry (<a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11945" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11945</a>).</p>
<pre data-v><code class="language-bash" data-v>bun x @foundry-rs/anvil --version
npx --yes @foundry-rs/cast --version
pnpm dlx --silent @foundry-rs/chisel --version
</code></pre>

<h2 data-v>Other</h2>
<ul data-v>
<li data-v>perf: reduce memory usage by boxing large error variants in wallet operations (#11928) by @Bilogweb3</li>

<h2 data-v>Full Changelog:</h2>
<p data-v><a href="https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/compare/v1.4.4...v1.5.1" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/compare/v1.4.4...v1.5.1</a></p></div></div></div></div></article></div></div></div><script>$RB=[];$RV=function(a){$RT=performance.now();for(var b=0;b<a.length;b+=2){var c=a[b],e=a[b+1];null!==e.parentNode&&e.parentNode.removeChild(e);var f=c.parentNode;if(f){var g=c.previousSibling,h=0;do{if(c&&8===c.nodeType){var d=c.data;if("/$"===d||"/&"===d)if(0===h)break;else h--;else"$"!==d&&"$?"!==d&&"$~"!==d&&"$!"!==d&&"&"!==d||h++}d=c.nextSibling;f.removeChild(c);c=d}while(c);for(;e.firstChild;)f.insertBefore(e.firstChild,c);g.data="$";g._reactRetry&&requestAnimationFrame(g._reactRetry)}}a.length=0};
$RC=function(a,b){if(b=document.getElementById(b))(a=document.getElementById(a))?(a.previousSibling.data="$~",$RB.push(a,b),2===$RB.length&&("number"!==typeof $RT?requestAnimationFrame($RV.bind(null,$RB)):(a=performance.now(),setTimeout($RV.bind(null,$RB),2300>a&&2E3<a?2300-a:$RT+300-a)))):b.parentNode.removeChild(b)};$RC("B:0","S:0")</script><script>(self.__FLIGHT_DATA||=[]).push("2:I[\"847a2b1045ef\",[],\"Slot\",1]\n3:I[\"3aa2a5f301a9\",[],\"Provider\",1]\n4:I[\"a649994c24a6\",[],\"Head\",1]\n5:I[\"5fed1ff16d81\",[],\"Main\",1]\n6:\"$Sreact.suspense\"\n7:I[\"c04e39735364\",[],\"Skeleton\",1]\n8:I[\"c04e39735364\",[],\"Changelog\",1]\n14:I[\"4cd9b2542026\",[],\"Root_client\",1]\n15:I[\"847a2b1045ef\",[],\"Children\",1]\n16:I[\"9b5d422c5822\",[],\"ScrollRestoration\",1]\n9:T4346,# Foundry v1.6.0\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.6.0 brings **Osaka as the default EVM hardfork**, major **performance improvements** with parallelized stateless fuzzing and configurable invariant check intervals (up to 3.6x faster deep runs), enhanced **security testing** with improved reentrancy detection and time-based invariant fuzzing, and additional **Tempo blockchain integration** across forge, cast, and anvil.\r\n\r\nWe recently crossed 10,000 GitHub ð â thank you to everyone who has contributed, reported issues, and helped improve Foundry!\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## Performance\r\n\r\n### Parallelized Stateless Fuzzing ([#12713](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12713))\r\n\r\nFuzz tests now run across multiple worker threads, significantly improving execution speed on multi-core machines. Each worker maintains its own corpus and periodically syncs with a master corpus, enabling efficient parallel exploration while sharing discovered coverage. Workers automatically distribute runs evenly and aggregate results after completion.\r\n\r\n### Invariant `check_interval` Config ([#13133](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13133))\r\n\r\nNew `check_interval` config option controls how often invariants are asserted during deep runs:\r\n\r\n| Value | Behavior |\r\n|-------|----------|\r\n| `0` | Only assert on the last call of each run (fastest) |\r\n| `1` (default) | Assert after every call (current behavior, most precise) |\r\n| `N` | Assert every N calls AND always on the last call |\r\n\r\n**Benchmark**: With `check_interval = 10`, deep invariant runs (1Ã1000 depth) are **3.6x faster** (15.09s â 4.17s). Invariant checks consume ~86% of execution time in high-depth runsâreducing check frequency dramatically improves performance while still catching violations.\r\n\r\n### Other Performance Improvements\r\n\r\n- perf: add dist profile for smaller release binaries ([#13097](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13097)) by @onbjerg\r\n- perf: compute literals only once ([#12716](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12716)) by @DaniPopes\r\n- perf: remove redundant allocation in receipt bloom calculation ([#13035](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13035)) by @marukai67\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## Security Testing\r\n\r\n### Improved Reentrancy Detection with `call_override` ([#13127](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13127))\r\n\r\nThe `call_override` invariant testing feature now correctly detects ETH transfer reentrancy vulnerabilities, including:\r\n- **EtherStore pattern**: Classic DAO-style reentrancy where a handler sends ETH out and the attacker reenters\r\n- **Rari Capital pattern**: Protocol-level reentrancy where external protocols send ETH to handlers\r\n\r\nKey fixes include proper ETH transfer via journal before callback injection, clearing REVM's cached bytecode for EOA targets, and overriding calls when either caller OR target is a handler contract. Validated against a reproduction of the April 2022 Rari Capital hack.\r\n\r\n### Time-based Invariant Fuzzing ([#12616](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12616))\r\n\r\nNew `max_time_delay` and `max_block_delay` invariant configs enable fuzzing of block timestamp and block number on consecutive transactions. This helps discover time-dependent vulnerabilities that only manifest under specific block timing conditions. Counterexamples now display the `vm.warp()` and `vm.roll()` calls needed to reproduce failures.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## Improved Integration\r\n\r\n### Foundry-toolchain TypeScript Rewrite\r\n\r\nThe [`foundry-toolchain`](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain) GitHub Action has been completely rewritten in TypeScript for improved maintainability and reliability. See [v1.7.0 release](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain/releases/tag/v1.7.0).\r\n\r\n### Foundryup Rust Rewrite (Experimental)\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.6.0 is accompanied by a new Rust rewrite of [`foundryup`](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundryup) for better maintainability, testing, and compatibility. At the moment the new `foundryup` installer is still experimental, but in next releases we plan to sunset the old one and provide a much better experience for managing foundry installs.\r\n\r\nTo try out the new `foundryup` run:\r\n\r\n```bash\r\ncurl -L https://raw.githubusercontent.com/foundry-rs/foundryup/HEAD/foundryup-init.sh | bash\r\nfoundryup\r\n```\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n## Network Changelog\r\n\r\n[v1.5.1...v1.6.0](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/compare/v1.5.1...v1.6.0-rc1)a:T56b0,<h1 data-v>Foundry v1.6.0</h1>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.6.0 brings <strong data-v>Osaka as the default EVM hardfork</strong>, major <strong data-v>performance improvements</strong> with parallelized stateless fuzzing and configurable invariant check intervals (up to 3.6x faster deep runs), enhanced <strong data-v>security testing</strong> with improved reentrancy detection and time-based invariant fuzzing, and additional <strong data-v>Tempo blockchain integration</strong> across forge, cast, and anvil.</p>\n<p data-v>We recently crossed 10,000 GitHub ð â thank you to everyone who has contributed, reported issues, and helped improve Foundry!</p>\n<hr data-v>\n<h2 data-v>Performance</h2>\n<h3 data-v>Parallelized Stateless Fuzzing (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12713\" data-v>#12713</a>)</h3>\n<p data-v>Fuzz tests now run across multiple worker threads, significantly improving execution speed on multi-core machines. Each worker maintains its own corpus and periodically syncs with a master corpus, enabling efficient parallel exploration while sharing discovered coverage. Workers automatically distribute runs evenly and aggregate results after completion.</p>\n<h3 data-v>Invariant <code data-v>check_interval</code> Config (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13133\" data-v>#13133</a>)</h3>\n<p data-v>New <code data-v>check_interval</code> config option controls how often invariants are asserted during deep runs:</p>\n<div data-v-table-wrapper><table data-v>\n<thead data-v>\n<tr data-v>\n<th data-v>Value</th>\n<th data-v>Behavior</th>\n</tr>\n</thead>\n<tbody data-v>\n<tr data-v>\n<td data-v><code data-v>0</code></td>\n<td data-v>Only assert on the last call of each run (fastest)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr data-v>\n<td data-v><code data-v>1</code> (default)</td>\n<td data-v>Assert after every call (current behavior, most precise)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr data-v>\n<td data-v><code data-v>N</code></td>\n<td data-v>Assert every N calls AND always on the last call</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table></div>\n<p data-v><strong data-v>Benchmark</strong>: With <code data-v>check_interval = 10</code>, deep invariant runs (1Ã1000 depth) are <strong data-v>3.6x faster</strong> (15.09s â 4.17s). Invariant checks consume ~86% of execution time in high-depth runsâreducing check frequency dramatically improves performance while still catching violations.</p>\n<h3 data-v>Other Performance Improvements</h3>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>perf: add dist profile for smaller release binaries (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13097\" data-v>#13097</a>) by @onbjerg</li>\n<li data-v>perf: compute literals only once (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12716\" data-v>#12716</a>) by @DaniPopes</li>\n<li data-v>perf: remove redundant allocation in receipt bloom calculation (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13035\" data-v>#13035</a>) by @marukai67</li>\n</ul>\n<hr data-v>\n<h2 data-v>Security Testing</h2>\n<h3 data-v>Improved Reentrancy Detection with <code data-v>call_override</code> (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13127\" data-v>#13127</a>)</h3>\n<p data-v>The <code data-v>call_override</code> invariant testing feature now correctly detects ETH transfer reentrancy vulnerabilities, including:</p>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v><strong data-v>EtherStore pattern</strong>: Classic DAO-style reentrancy where a handler sends ETH out and the attacker reenters</li>\n<li data-v><strong data-v>Rari Capital pattern</strong>: Protocol-level reentrancy where external protocols send ETH to handlers</li>\n</ul>\n<p data-v>Key fixes include proper ETH transfer via journal before callback injection, clearing REVM's cached bytecode for EOA targets, and overriding calls when either caller OR target is a handler contract. Validated against a reproduction of the April 2022 Rari Capital hack.</p>\n<h3 data-v>Time-based Invariant Fuzzing (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12616\" data-v>#12616</a>)</h3>\n<p data-v>New <code data-v>max_time_delay</code> and <code data-v>max_block_delay</code> invariant configs enable fuzzing of block timestamp and block number on consecutive transactions. This helps discover time-dependent vulnerabilities that only manifest under specific block timing conditions. Counterexamples now display the <code data-v>vm.warp()</code> and <code data-v>vm.roll()</code> calls needed to reproduce failures.</p>\n<hr data-v>\n<h2 data-v>Improved Integration</h2>\n<h3 data-v>Foundry-toolchain TypeScript Rewrite</h3>\n<p data-v>The <a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain\" data-v><code data-v>foundry-toolchain</code></a> GitHub Action has been completely rewritten in TypeScript for improved maintainability and reliability. See <a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-toolchain/releases/tag/v1.7.0\" data-v>v1.7.0 release</a>.</p>\n<h3 data-v>Foundryup Rust Rewrite (Experimental)</h3>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.6.0 is accompanied by a new Rust rewrite of <a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundryup\" data-v><code data-v>foundryup</code></a> for better maintainability, testing, and compatibility. At the moment the new <code data-v>foundryup</code> installer is still experimental, but in next releases we plan to sunset the old one and provide a much better experience for managing foundry installs.</p>\n<p data-v>To try out the new <code data-v>foundryup</code> run:</p>\n<pre data-v><code class=\"language-bash\" data-v>curl -L https://raw.githubusercontent.com/foundry-rs/foundryup/HEAD/foundryup-init.sh | bash\r\nfoundryup\n</code></pre>\n<hr data-v>\n<h2 data-v>Network Updates</h2>\n<h3 data-v>Tempo Blockchain Integration</h3>\n<p data-v>Additional Tempo network support is now available across the Foundry toolchain:</p>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>feat(forge): add <code data-v>--network tempo</code> flag to <code data-v>forge init</code> (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12819\" data-v>#12819</a>) by @onbjerg - Initialize projects pre-configured for Tempo</li>\n<li data-v>feat(cast): tempo nonce keys (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12977\" data-v>#12977</a>) by @onbjerg - Support for Tempo's nonce key system</li>\n<li data-v>feat(cast): add tempo tx construction support (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12973\" data-v>#12973</a>) by @onbjerg - Build and sign Tempo transactions</li>\n<li data-v>feat(anvil): basic tempo tx signing support (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12974\" data-v>#12974</a>) by @onbjerg - Local development with Tempo transactions</li>\n<li data-v>feat(<code data-v>foundryup</code>): add Tempo support (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12775\" data-v>#12775</a>) by @zerosnacks - Install Tempo-enabled Foundry builds</li>\n</ul>\n<h3 data-v>Chain Support</h3>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>feat: add XDC Network + SKALE Base support by bumping <code data-v>alloy-chains</code> (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12710\" data-v>#12710</a>) by @zerosnacks</li>\n<li data-v>feat: use different gas calc for monad mainnet (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12615\" data-v>#12615</a>) by @QEDK</li>\n<li data-v>fix: use network-specific BaseFeeParams for Optimism in Anvil (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12944\" data-v>#12944</a>) by @haythemsellami</li>\n</ul>\n<hr data-v>\n<h2 data-v>Forge</h2>\n<h3 data-v>Features</h3>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>feat: use Osaka as default EVM hardfork (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/13112\" data-v>#13112</a>) by @zerosnacks</li>\n<li data-v>feat(forge selectors): cache selectors from abis (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12742\" data-v>#12742</a>) by @JuaniRios</li>\n<li data-v>feat(forge href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/compare/v1.5.1...v1.6.0-rc1\" data-v>v1.5.1...v1.6.0</a></p>b:T6f8b,# Foundry v1.5.1\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.5.1 is a bugfix release to support solc 0.8.31.\r\n\r\n- fix: backport svm rs bump to 1.5.1 / stable (#12871) by @grandizzy\r\n\r\n# Foundry v1.5.0\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.5.0 release comes with an improved fuzzer that use [`Solar`](https://github.com/paradigmxyz/solar) to analyze contracts and extract interested values from AST, and incorporate updated logic to minimize counterexamples generated by invariant tests. This version adds support for browser extension wallets, provides a simpler way to interact with ERC20 tokens using cast and publishes all foundry binaries as npm packages. It also continues the effort to improve new forge formatter rolled out in previous version and makes it more customizable.\r\n\r\n## Fuzzed tests improvements\r\n\r\n### AST seeded dictionary\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.5.0 leverages the Solar API to analyze contracts, collect all relevant AST literals from the sources, and use those values to generate inputs for the fuzzing campaign (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12015).\r\nFor example, with this addition a counterexample for the simple test below can be generated within a couple of runs:  \r\n```Solidity\r\nfunction testHash(bytes memory v) external {\r\n    assert(keccak256(v) != keccak256(\"hello\"));\r\n}\r\n```\r\nEarly testers have reported substantially improved fuzzing results and we are running additional benchmarks to quantify the effectiveness.\r\n\r\n### Improved counterexample shrinking\r\n\r\nIn previous versions, counterexamples generated by invariant tests were replayed and minimized only once. In Foundry v1.5.0, the call sequence is replayed multiple times until all configured shrink runs are completed (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12180). Additionally, the counterexamples saved on disk and replayed on subsequent campaigns, are now also minimized (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12351). This allows Foundry to produce a more thoroughly minimized call sequence that can be used to generate unit tests and reproduce smart contract invariant violations.\r\n\r\n## Browser wallet integration\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.5.0 introduces support for browser extension wallets in the `cast send` and `cast wallet sign` commands, enabling developers to sign transactions directly in the browser (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12302). Future releases will expand browser wallet support to other Foundry commands. We look forward to get external contributions to improve [the interface](https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-browser-wallet) and feature set of the browser wallet.\r\n\r\nTo try it out, pass the `--browser` flag to `cast send` to send a transaction using any of your browser wallets: `cast send <TO> --value <VALUE> --rpc-url <RPC_URL> --browser`\r\n\r\n<p align=\"center\">\r\n  <img width=\"441\" height=\"492\" alt=\"Porto send\" src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/850a2108-15e1-484c-987f-208b3c2ececf\" />\r\n</p>\r\n\r\nAdditionally you can sign messages and typed data with `cast wallet sign`: `cast wallet sign --browser \"Hello World!\"`\r\n<p align=\"center\">\r\n  <img width=\"441\" height=\"492\" alt=\"Porto Sign\" src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/2ff1fbbc-b565-4182-9993-6c640783c575\" />\r\n</p>\r\n\r\n\r\n## ERC20 support in cast\r\n\r\nThis release introduces the `cast erc20` command to facilitate interaction with ERC-20 tokens (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12258 https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12381). This makes it simple to query balances, perform transfers, and access other ERC-20 token details.\r\n```bash\r\n  balance       Query ERC20 token balance [aliases: b]\r\n  transfer      Transfer ERC20 tokens [aliases: t]\r\n  approve       Approve ERC20 token spending [aliases: a]\r\n  allowance     Query ERC20 token allowance [aliases: al]\r\n  name          Query ERC20 token name [aliases: n]\r\n  symbol        Query ERC20 token symbol [aliases: s]\r\n  decimals      Query ERC20 token decimals [aliases: d]\r\n  total-supply  Query ERC20 token total supply [aliases: ts]\r\n  mint          Mint ERC20 tokens (if the token supports minting) [aliases: m]\r\n  burn          Burn ERC20 tokens [aliases: bu]\r\n```\r\n\r\n## New cheatcodes\r\n\r\nFoundry v1.5.0 includes a set of new cheatcodes designed to improve the testing experience:\r\n- `getEvmVersion/setEvmVersion` to retrieve and change the execution EVM version within tests and scripts (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12014)\r\n- `signWithNonce` to create deterministic ECDSA signatures using a specified ephemeral nonce (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11267)\r\n- `getStorageSlots` leverage the storage layout to accurately identify the base slot of a variable (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11537)\r\n\r\n## npm packages\r\n\r\nContinuing the work introduced in v1.4.0 for `forge`, v1.5.0 publishes the remaining Foundry binaries as npm packages. This allows tools such as `bun`, `npx`, `pnpm` to easily install and run any Foundry executable directly from the npm registry (https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11945). \r\n```bash\r\nbun x @foundry-rs/anvil --version\r\nnpx --yes @foundry-rs/cast --version\r\npnpm dlx --silent @foundry-rs/chisel --version\r\n```\r\n\r\n## Performance Improvements\r\n\r\n- perf(evm): reduce rpc calls when instantiating a fork environment (#12145) by @DaniPopes\r\n- perf: remove some more unnecessary RPC calls (#12338) by @DaniPopes\r\n\r\n## Anvil Features\r\n\r\n- feat(anvil): wire eth_protocolVersion, eth_hashrate, eth_coinbase RPCs (#11934) by @sashass1315\r\n- perf(anvil): optimize internal data passing in log queries (#11896) by @silvekkk\r\n- feat(anvil): add `/eth/v1/beacon/blobs` beacon endpoint (#12182) by @mablr\r\n- feat(anvil): add `debug_dbGet` endpoint (#12375) by @mablr\r\n- perf(anvil): avoid unnecessary transaction vector cloning in Block::new (#12393) by @CreeptoGengar\r\n- feat(anvil): Implement alloy_evm `FromRecoveredTx` trait for anvil `TypedTransaction` (#12424) by @mablr\r\n- perf(anvil): avoid snapshot cloning when counting ready transactions (#12432) by @phrwlk\r\n- fix(anvil): set evm block number to input value (#12490) by @Syzygy106\r\n- feat(anvil): handle signature impersonation for EIP-7702 authorization list (#12553) by @mablr\r\n\r\n## Anvil Fixes\r\n\r\n- anvil: remove unused BlockNumberOrTag import in hardfork tests (#11952) by @anim001k\r\n- fix: use blobparams for blob fee calc (#12056) by @mattsse\r\n- fix(anvil): set envelope for non deposit tx in debug tracers (#12080) by @grandizzy\r\n- fix(anvil): eth_getAccountInfo check if predates fork inclusive (#12101) by @grandizzy\r\n- fix(anvil): always disable nonce check for `eth_call`s (#12144) by @grandizzy\r\n- fix(anvil): get account info from db when node block > fork block (#12175) by @grandizzy\r\n- fix(anvil): remove transactions before @grandizzy\r\n\r\n## Full Changelog:\r\n https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/compare/v1.4.4...v1.5.1c:T8933,<h1 data-v>Foundry v1.5.1</h1>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.1 is a bugfix release to support solc 0.8.31.</p>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>fix: backport svm rs bump to 1.5.1 / stable (#12871) by @grandizzy</li>\n</ul>\n<h1 data-v>Foundry v1.5.0</h1>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 release comes with an improved fuzzer that use <a href=\"https://github.com/paradigmxyz/solar\" data-v><code data-v>Solar</code></a> to analyze contracts and extract interested values from AST, and incorporate updated logic to minimize counterexamples generated by invariant tests. This version adds support for browser extension wallets, provides a simpler way to interact with ERC20 tokens using cast and publishes all foundry binaries as npm packages. It also continues the effort to improve new forge formatter rolled out in previous version and makes it more customizable.</p>\n<h2 data-v>Fuzzed tests improvements</h2>\n<h3 data-v>AST seeded dictionary</h3>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 leverages the Solar API to analyze contracts, collect all relevant AST literals from the sources, and use those values to generate inputs for the fuzzing campaign (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12015\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12015</a>).\r\nFor example, with this addition a counterexample for the simple test below can be generated within a couple of runs:</p>\n<pre data-v><code class=\"language-Solidity\" data-v>function testHash(bytes memory v) external {\r\n    assert(keccak256(v) != keccak256(\"hello\"));\r\n}\n</code></pre>\n<p data-v>Early testers have reported substantially improved fuzzing results and we are running additional benchmarks to quantify the effectiveness.</p>\n<h3 data-v>Improved counterexample shrinking</h3>\n<p data-v>In previous versions, counterexamples generated by invariant tests were replayed and minimized only once. In Foundry v1.5.0, the call sequence is replayed multiple times until all configured shrink runs are completed (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12180\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12180</a>). Additionally, the counterexamples saved on disk and replayed on subsequent campaigns, are now also minimized (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12351\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12351</a>). This allows Foundry to produce a more thoroughly minimized call sequence that can be used to generate unit tests and reproduce smart contract invariant violations.</p>\n<h2 data-v>Browser wallet integration</h2>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 introduces support for browser extension wallets in the <code data-v>cast send</code> and <code data-v>cast wallet sign</code> commands, enabling developers to sign transactions directly in the browser (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12302\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12302</a>). Future releases will expand browser wallet support to other Foundry commands. We look forward to get external contributions to improve <a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry-browser-wallet\" data-v>the interface</a> and feature set of the browser wallet.</p>\n<p data-v>To try it out, pass the <code data-v>--browser</code> flag to <code data-v>cast send</code> to send a transaction using any of your browser wallets: <code data-v>cast send &#x3C;TO> --value &#x3C;VALUE> --rpc-url &#x3C;RPC_URL> --browser</code></p>\n<p align=\"center\">\r\n  <img width=\"441\" height=\"492\" alt=\"Porto send\" src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/850a2108-15e1-484c-987f-208b3c2ececf\" />\r\n</p>\n<p data-v>Additionally you can sign messages and typed data with <code data-v>cast wallet sign</code>: <code data-v>cast wallet sign --browser \"Hello World!\"</code></p>\n<p align=\"center\">\r\n  <img width=\"441\" height=\"492\" alt=\"Porto Sign\" src=\"https://github.com/user-attachments/assets/2ff1fbbc-b565-4182-9993-6c640783c575\" />\r\n</p>\n<h2 data-v>ERC20 support in cast</h2>\n<p data-v>This release introduces the <code data-v>cast erc20</code> command to facilitate interaction with ERC-20 tokens (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12258\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12258</a> <a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12381\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12381</a>). This makes it simple to query balances, perform transfers, and access other ERC-20 token details.</p>\n<pre data-v><code class=\"language-bash\" data-v>  balance       Query ERC20 token balance [aliases: b]\r\n  transfer      Transfer ERC20 tokens [aliases: t]\r\n  approve       Approve ERC20 token spending [aliases: a]\r\n  allowance     Query ERC20 token allowance [aliases: al]\r\n  name          Query ERC20 token name [aliases: n]\r\n  symbol        Query ERC20 token symbol [aliases: s]\r\n  decimals      Query ERC20 token decimals [aliases: d]\r\n  total-supply  Query ERC20 token total supply [aliases: ts]\r\n  mint          Mint ERC20 tokens (if the token supports minting) [aliases: m]\r\n  burn          Burn ERC20 tokens [aliases: bu]\n</code></pre>\n<h2 data-v>New cheatcodes</h2>\n<p data-v>Foundry v1.5.0 includes a set of new cheatcodes designed to improve the testing experience:</p>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v><code data-v>getEvmVersion/setEvmVersion</code> to retrieve and change the execution EVM version within tests and scripts (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12014\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/12014</a>)</li>\n<li data-v><code data-v>signWithNonce</code> to create deterministic ECDSA signatures using a specified ephemeral nonce (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11267\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11267</a>)</li>\n<li data-v><code data-v>getStorageSlots</code> leverage the storage layout to accurately identify the base slot of a variable (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11537\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11537</a>)</li>\n</ul>\n<h2 data-v>npm packages</h2>\n<p data-v>Continuing the work introduced in v1.4.0 for <code data-v>forge</code>, v1.5.0 publishes the remaining Foundry binaries as npm packages. This allows tools such as <code data-v>bun</code>, <code data-v>npx</code>, <code data-v>pnpm</code> to easily install and run any Foundry executable directly from the npm registry (<a href=\"https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11945\" data-v>https://github.com/foundry-rs/foundry/pull/11945</a>).</p>\n<pre data-v><code class=\"language-bash\" data-v>bun x @foundry-rs/anvil --version\r\nnpx --yes @foundry-rs/cast --version\r\npnpm dlx --silent @foundry-rs/chisel --version\n</code></pre>\n<h2 data-v>Performance Improvements</h2>\n<ul data-v>\n<li data-v>perf(evm): reduce
